<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_cf5015fd-d96d-4b67-95c5-95637d4d6147'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

</script>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer968005578" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6578871292334685892"><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1429550074i/14604012._SY540_.jpg' width='400' height='577' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>Most of my life, I've hated the news. Honestly I avoided it like the plague. Every station, every minute, seemed to be inundated with murder, abuse, injustice. I couldn’t stand it. So I refused to watch. I stuck my head in the sand, and chose to pretend that terrible things weren’t happening every day. <br/><br/><i>
  <b>I have a complex, sure. But it’s more of an I hate humans thing. Disappointed. I am so disappointed in people. It’s like they live without souls.</b>
</i><br/><br/>Reading Tarryn’s post about what drove her to </span>
  <span id="freeText6578871292334685892" style="display:none"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1429550074i/14604012._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="577" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Most of my life, I've hated the news. Honestly I avoided it like the plague. Every station, every minute, seemed to be inundated with murder, abuse, injustice. I couldn’t stand it. So I refused to watch. I stuck my head in the sand, and chose to pretend that terrible things weren’t happening every day. <br><br><i>
  <b>I have a complex, sure. But it’s more of an I hate humans thing. Disappointed. I am so disappointed in people. It’s like they live without souls.</b>
</i><br><br>Reading Tarryn’s post about what drove her to write this story, well it was a bit of a slap in the face. The world is not always a pretty place. Victims deserve to have their story told, I felt ashamed for all the stories I’ve avoided over the years. <br><br><i>
  <b>I hate that nothing can be done about the suffering of children, and that most of the world blocks out their suffering to cope with their own inability to help.</b>
</i><br><br><i>Marrow</i> is the story of a young girl who has seen injustice, who has watched the innocent suffer, but in her neighborhood there are no hero’s, they are poor and ignored. Margo has had enough, she decides to take matters into her own hands. <br><br><i>
  <b>I do not kill just because. I execute the wicked. People who had no place living, sharing the planet with those of us trying to survive— making it harder.</b>
</i><br><br>To be perfectly honest, I have struggled with how to review this, I don't want to give anything away. And my head is still spinning. This story made me feel. If you enjoy dark, suspenseful, psychological thrillers, I definitely recommend this one. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1429629660i/14613882._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="263" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>*Note - I wouldn't consider this a romance, so if you are looking for a sweet, smutty or angsty romance, you will not find it in this story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6578871292334685892" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3331895953249622469"><br/>Tarryn Fisher’s <i>Marrow</i> is like no other. Market saturated with romance formula books--<i>Marrow</i> will completely rock your world and make you question the very reason why you became a reader. Absolutely bone chilling. Tarryn’s precise, spare prose cuts you like a knife, breaking you open, shattering you, and making you all sorts of uncomfortable with the dark truths of the world and Margo's quest for righteousness. There is nothing comfortable and settling about <i>Marrow</i>, if you are looking for the pr</span>
  <span id="freeText3331895953249622469" style="display:none"><br>Tarryn Fisher’s <i>Marrow</i> is like no other. Market saturated with romance formula books--<i>Marrow</i> will completely rock your world and make you question the very reason why you became a reader. Absolutely bone chilling. Tarryn’s precise, spare prose cuts you like a knife, breaking you open, shattering you, and making you all sorts of uncomfortable with the dark truths of the world and Margo's quest for righteousness. There is nothing comfortable and settling about <i>Marrow</i>, if you are looking for the predictable, look elsewhere. Margo is a much-needed heroine, Judah a breath of fresh air. <i>Marrow</i> will fill you with despair and pick you up with justice, dark humor, and unquestionable hope. <br><br><br>so you will not miss the cat...<br><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1399127945ra/9511805.gif" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<div id="review_944555754" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/944555754" />
    <a title="Jennifer Kyle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9916227-jennifer-kyle"><img alt="Jennifer Kyle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514915429p2/9916227.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/944555754?book_show_action=true">May 21, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer Kyle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer Kyle" href="/user/show/9916227-jennifer-kyle">Jennifer Kyle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9916227-jennifer-kyle?shelf=i-like-it-dark-and-twisted">i-like-it-dark-and-twisted</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer944555754" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer75361307710204106"><b>3.5 Stars</b><br/><br/>(Not sure how to star: First Half ~ 4 Stars / Second Half ~ 2 Stars ~ Writing 5 Stars)<br/><br/><b>
  <i>”The Bone is in our marrow. It’s complacency and fear handed down from generation to generation.”</i>
</b><br/><br/><span>[image error]</span> <br/><br/>Tarryn Fisher delivered a well written and graphically dark tale that has a likable heroine, Margo who lives in the Bone Harbor. The Bone and all its inhabitants are expertly written and depicted. These characters are very poor while embracing their addictions and all the while their child</span>
  <span id="freeText75361307710204106" style="display:none"><b>3.5 Stars</b><br><br>(Not sure how to star: First Half ~ 4 Stars / Second Half ~ 2 Stars ~ Writing 5 Stars)<br><br><b>
  <i>”The Bone is in our marrow. It’s complacency and fear handed down from generation to generation.”</i>
</b><br><br><span>[image error]</span> <br><br>Tarryn Fisher delivered a well written and graphically dark tale that has a likable heroine, Margo who lives in the Bone Harbor. The Bone and all its inhabitants are expertly written and depicted. These characters are very poor while embracing their addictions and all the while their children grow to be adults themselves. <br><br><b>
  <i>”I imagine that being wanted is the greatest feeling. A feeling that solidifies your stay in this life, justifies it.”</i>
</b><br> <br>Margo lives with her mother in the “eating house”. Margo a once overweight and invisible girl has to face losses and reveals after her high school graduation. She finds a relationship with the handicap sweetheart of her neighborhood, Judah.<br> <br><b>
  <i>”A friendship between the fat, ugly girl and the crippled, handsome boy. It is a friendship that we both had waited for. One we both needed.”</i>
</b><br><br>The story has murders, child abuse and some twists and turns along the way. The story takes on a new light slowly as Margo finds strength in delivering justice and becomes a vigilante of sorts.<br><br><b>
  <i>”I don’t want to hurt people, I don’t have an innate need to, but they must be punished. That’s what I do, or what I tell myself I do. I punish. I feel responsible for it. An eye for an eye. A beating for a beating. A burn for a burn. I have a conscience. It is different from the conscience of the average person, but at least it’s there. It is there, isn’t it?”</i>
</b><br><br>Once out of Bone Harbor, Margo makes a new life for herself until she senses injustice and feels called to stand up for those who can’t. This is where the author will throw her twist at a reader and connection to the prior book.<br> <br>I enjoyed the first forty or so percent of this book and for me there wasn’t much of a love story at all, just a tease of one amongst the pages but a love for victims everywhere. I would have preferred that the story have gone in a different direction in the middle (If I understand what the ending meant correctly- perhaps I didn’t?). The writing was intriguingly dark and deep, the main character will hold your attention and wish for more for her and the author does shoot for a “mind fuck” not sure if she truly pulls it off. <br><br>Now for the big question: Will my Goodread friends like this one? <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1492484694ra/22521325.gif" width="390" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>I think if friends loved Mud Vein than you will be thrilled with this book. If you made it to the end of Mud Vein with out dnfing then you will like this one much more. This was a step better than Mud Vein for me but is it wrong to have wished Colleen Hoover collaborated on it? <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1492484694ra/22521327.gif" width="390" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> </span>
  <a data-text-id="75361307710204106" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1081888941" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1081888941" />
    <a title="✦❋Arianna✦❋" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23370948-arianna"><img alt="✦❋Arianna✦❋" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1420671997p2/23370948.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1081888941?book_show_action=true">Oct 16, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="✦❋Arianna✦❋" class="user" itemprop="url" name="✦❋Arianna✦❋" href="/user/show/23370948-arianna">✦❋Arianna✦❋</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23370948-arianna?shelf=dark-romance">dark-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1081888941" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3747000958516145319"><b>3.5-4 Stars</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1429709209i/14622792._SY540_.jpg' width='400' height='550' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>”The Bone is in our marrow. It’s complacency and fear handed down from generation to generation.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><br/>If you’re looking for a sweet romance you will not find it reading this book. This is definitely not a love story. A story about love? Yes...maybe...I don’t know. Depends how you see certain aspects of the story. For me it was a dark, twisted and confusing psychological thriller that messed up a little with my head. <i>“Marrow”</i> is a story about life, love, vengeance, justice and s</span>
  <span id="freeText3747000958516145319" style="display:none"><b>3.5-4 Stars</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1429709209i/14622792._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="550" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>”The Bone is in our marrow. It’s complacency and fear handed down from generation to generation.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>If you’re looking for a sweet romance you will not find it reading this book. This is definitely not a love story. A story about love? Yes...maybe...I don’t know. Depends how you see certain aspects of the story. For me it was a dark, twisted and confusing psychological thriller that messed up a little with my head. <i>“Marrow”</i> is a story about life, love, vengeance, justice and so much more. It’s a very graphic story. It’s real. And it’s even eye opening. It’s a story that will make you reflect and it’s a story that will make you question everything.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“The eating house will never stop calling to me, and I will never cease to answer.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>The story is about Margo Moon, a girl who grow up in a bad neighborhood. She lives with her mother in the <i>“eating house”</i> in a small town, Bone. Over the years her mother becomes an agoraphobic, paranoid, pill-addicted prostitute so needless to say, Margo’s life is not easy. Her mother is not abusive, but she’s kinda of controlling. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“People do bad things in the dark, under the hollow gaze of the moon. It’s smiling at me now, proud of my sin. I’m not proud. I’m not anything. An eye for an eye, I tell myself. A beating for a beating.“</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>Margo is surrounded only by ugliness and injustice. Tired to see so much suffering, she decides to take matters into her own hands. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I do not kill just because. I execute the wicked. People who had no place living, sharing the planet with those of us trying to survive— making it harder.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1429709209i/14622793._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="553" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Margo meets Judah, a boy from the neighborhood and they become friends. Eventually she starts to want more than a simple friendship with him.<br> <br>The characters of this story are complex, flawed and maybe real in some way as well. At first Margo is timid and afraid, but as the story progresses and she sees how cruel and ugly the world she lives in can be she changes. Practically she becomes another girl – determined, fearless, <i>“something deadly”</i>,ruthless. I think Margo is that king of character you will love to hate and hate to love. She’s not a psychopath and she’s not portrayed like one. She can feel happiness, sadness, she can sympathize with others. When she kills for the first time she doesn’t actually wants to kill. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“An eye for an eye. A beating for a beating. A burn for a burn. I have a conscience. It is different from the conscience of the average person, but at least it’s there.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>And she does have a conscience. Even if she continues to kill.<br> <br>I felt for Margo, I really did. She’s such a lonely girl. She thinks she’s not worth loving, that she’s not worth fighting, but Judah tries to make her see that she’s wrong, tries to make her see her own beauty. Not only her physical beauty. This boy, Judah is Margo’s only light and beauty in the world. He’s the only one who believes in her, who accepts her, who cares for her. He represents the light and hope in Margo’s world. Margo is strong and she is smart. She represents the good as much as she represents the bad. Many readers will agree with all her actions. Is she wrong to be the only judge? Is she right? Personally, I don’t know. I’m still not sure.<br><br>Like I mentioned before the story is confusing. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Who is Judah? Is he real? - Well, to find out you will have to read the book!:D <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>There are some interesting twists, but for me nothing was too spectacular. While I liked this story, I didn’t love it. It didn’t wow me and I felt like something was missing. What? I’m still not sure.<br><br>I think the ending represents the message of the entire book?!?I'm not sure..<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[You can’t run from who you are. You have to accept who and what you are, you have to embrace it. You can’t run away from your marrow. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>This is just a guess..<br><br>Overall, a great read!</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="3747000958516145319" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1257832589" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1257832589" />
    <a title="Tough Critic Book Reviews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5336035-tough-critic-book-reviews"><img alt="Tough Critic Book Reviews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1345668583p2/5336035.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1257832589?book_show_action=true">Apr 18, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tough Critic Book Reviews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tough Critic Book Reviews" href="/user/show/5336035-tough-critic-book-reviews">Tough Critic Book Reviews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1257832589" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11392410834617821065">There is a psychotic intelligence to Tarryn Fisher's writing. It's infectious. It's intrusive. It's folie á deux, contagious insanity. It's manipulative in a way that reflects genius. That is what I loved most about <i>Marrow</i>. Even her descriptives give life to the most mundane things. Noises. Objects. It's described in a way that gives any, and everything, a soul. <i>Marrow</i> is a living, breathing thing that will invade your mind, rearrange the furniture, then blow it up. <br/><br/>Parts of me craved a bit more</span>
  <span id="freeText11392410834617821065" style="display:none">There is a psychotic intelligence to Tarryn Fisher's writing. It's infectious. It's intrusive. It's folie á deux, contagious insanity. It's manipulative in a way that reflects genius. That is what I loved most about <i>Marrow</i>. Even her descriptives give life to the most mundane things. Noises. Objects. It's described in a way that gives any, and everything, a soul. <i>Marrow</i> is a living, breathing thing that will invade your mind, rearrange the furniture, then blow it up. <br /><br />Parts of me craved a bit more character interaction, but instead I found myself imprisoned inside the mind of Margo Moon. The hero? The villain? The other. Tarryn Fisher's characters surpass all labels. It is never black and white. It's all about perception. With <i>Marrow</i>, no two readers are going to read the same story. I'll admit, I did find some things confusing, leaving me with unanswered questions, but I can't help assuming that was the intent, part of the premeditated psychosis that is beyond my comprehension. That is the genius.<br /><br />This is what sets Tarryn Fisher's novels apart from the formulated influx of fantastical romance novels where the characters' farts smell of love and promises. This is its own genre of fiction. <br /><br />Some will say that love is definitely a minor theme in <i>Marrow</i>. If talking about the love between Judah and Margo, I agree, but love <i>is</i> the central theme. Margo's love for something far more dark. Something, that by the end of the novel, I not only understood, but condoned. Calling her a vigilante would be far too simple. Obsession. Vengeance. Justice. Whatever the motivation, she loved too much. The intent that created Margo, was emotional and deeper than any one word such as love could adequately describe. So for me, in some truly messed up way, this story had a "Happily Ever After."<br /><br />But for you, you'll have to read it to decide. <br /><br />READ ON!</span>
  <a data-text-id="11392410834617821065" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText13875064426296209293" style="display:none"><b>I read this in 2015 and it still sticks with me now, 2019. It’s just a hard-hitting brilliant book. One of my favourite books of all time. In fact, read all her books!</b><br><br><b>My Review.</b><br><br>This is a very emotional moment...one of the only books to render me speechless and unable to formulate a detailed review.<br><br>I actually read and finished this book back in early November, it's now nearly the end of 2015 and I have simply been unable to write a review of this book as it's just so darn emotional. <div id="review_1257808673" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1257808673" />
    <a title="Peek At My Book Review" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18263404-peek-at-my-book-review"><img alt="Peek At My Book Review" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1414761368p2/18263404.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1257808673?book_show_action=true">Apr 17, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Peek At My Book Review" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Peek At My Book Review" href="/user/show/18263404-peek-at-my-book-review">Peek At My Book Review</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18263404-peek-at-my-book-review?shelf=2015">2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1257808673" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14662647120993306527"><b>Rating : 3.5 ‘pink Zippo’ Stars</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1430143314i/14685779._SY540_.jpg' width='400"' height='771' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><i>Please note that this review is solely my opinion, you may or may not agree with what is being said.</i><br/><br/><b>My Views :</b> I liked this book but was a little <b> disappointed.</b> <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1381219138ra/4552184.gif' width='40' height='40' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> I really loved Mud Vein by this author and despite the depth that we get in Marrow, this book didn’t enthrall me like a Tarryn Fisher’s book normally does. After reading her Facebook status about how she began reading this book, I was <b> intrigued </b> <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1430146331ra/14686079.gif' width='40' height='40' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> and stopped everything to read this one but it just didn’t </span>
  <span id="freeText14662647120993306527" style="display:none"><b>Rating : 3.5 ‘pink Zippo’ Stars</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1430143314i/14685779._SY540_.jpg" width='400"' height="771" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Please note that this review is solely my opinion, you may or may not agree with what is being said.</i><br><br><b>My Views :</b> I liked this book but was a little <b> disappointed.</b> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1381219138ra/4552184.gif" width="40" height="40" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> I really loved Mud Vein by this author and despite the depth that we get in Marrow, this book didn’t enthrall me like a Tarryn Fisher’s book normally does. After reading her Facebook status about how she began reading this book, I was <b> intrigued </b> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1430146331ra/14686079.gif" width="40" height="40" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> and stopped everything to read this one but it just didn’t feel right. What I loved was the town ‘Bone’, I loved how she portrayed Bone, the residents and their lives or lack of. But I felt the story was <b> too straining and dragging…</b><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1430146331ra/14686080.gif" width="40" height="40" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> I started skimming the pages after 50%. Then after 80% the story picked up again.<br><br><b>Style of writing :</b> I have always been a fan of Tarryn Fisher.<b> She has a way of weaving her stories in my core. </b> Even though the story didn’t blew me, I still loved her writing. But sometimes it can be straining to the brain. However, at times there were huge chuck which were only monologues, sometime there was only narration…absolutely no dialogues which had me <b> flipping the pages. </b> Her writing at times reminded me of V.Woolf, not going into the stream of consciousness but jumping from one event to another. The story for me was written in a Woolf style (we get snapshops of events) but the ending was a<b> Dickensian Ending or let’s say Tarryn Fisher’s Justice. </b> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1430146331ra/14686081.gif" width="40" height="40" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1430146331i/14686083._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="550" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Characters :</b> Maybe that was the author’s intention but I couldn’t connect with the characters. They were all so distant. I am disappointed that I couldn’t even connect with Margo even though this book was from her perspective. I do understand Margo’s need to bring justice to innocents but there is still a mysterious part of her than even given her pov, we can decifer. And somewhere near the end I lost her, I could no longer point out what was real and what was not. <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1430146331ra/14686082.gif" width="40" height="40" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><b>Favorite Part :</b> None..<br><br><b>What did not work?</b> Hmm..I just couldn’t connect with this one. I’m definitely going to read more from this author but this one didn’t really work for me.<br><br><b> Similar books? </b> None that I’ve read so far…<br><br><b> Recommended :</b> If you’re a fan of Tarryn Fisher and her writing then yes…Note that this book does <b>NOT</b> contain much romance.<br><br><b>For more reviews check my blog</b><br><a href="http://peekatmybookreview.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img alt="description" height="150" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1427460776i/14272326._SX540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <br><a href="https://twitter.com/theVrsha" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img alt="description" height="60" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1418815952i/12909809.png" width="60" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/theVrsha/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img alt="description" height="60" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1425728890i/13923816.jpg" width="60" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <a href="https://www.facebook.com/pages/Peek-At-My-Book-Review/313910035485042?ref=hl" rel="nofollow noopener">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1260020109?book_show_action=true">Apr 20, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelly (and the Book Boar)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelly (and the Book Boar)" href="/user/show/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar">Kelly (and the Book Boar)</a>

        rated it

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1260020109" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4708241275979150851">Find all of my reviews at: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/'>http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br/><br/><b>
  <i>“People will ignore every warning sign when blinded by their thirst for something. It’s better to not be thirsty.”</i>
</b><br/><br/><a href='http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/texas/houston/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1440168493ra/15940065.gif' alt='Houston commercial photography' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Well, this was an unexpected little surprise. Tarryn Fisher went on my radar with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1194522493?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>Mud Vein </a>, a book that promised to be über dark and disturbing and yada yada yada. It didn’t work for me, but I enjoyed the writing style and thought she definitely had the potential with the doom and gloom. She also didn’t seem to be </span>
  <span id="freeText4708241275979150851" style="display:none">Find all of my reviews at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/">http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br><br><b>
  <i>“People will ignore every warning sign when blinded by their thirst for something. It’s better to not be thirsty.”</i>
</b><br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/texas/houston/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1440168493ra/15940065.gif" alt="Houston commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Well, this was an unexpected little surprise. Tarryn Fisher went on my radar with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1194522493?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Mud Vein </a>, a book that promised to be über dark and disturbing and yada yada yada. It didn’t work for me, but I enjoyed the writing style and thought she definitely had the potential with the doom and gloom. She also didn’t seem to be an a$$hole when I saw her posting on social media which was a huge bonus. When Amazon offered me up a free $5 gift card I knew exactly what I would be spending it on. Boy am I glad I did. <br><br><i>Marrow</i> is classified under the “New Adult” genre, but it’s not your typical NA story . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/texas/houston/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1440168493ra/15940066.gif" alt="Houston commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>This isn’t a romance. (Well, I mean if you’re a person who would categorize <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/824864992?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">American Psycho</a> as a romance I guess it could be.) Nope, <i>Marrow</i> is the story of what happens when Margo has enough with living in “The Bone” – enough with being raised by a prostitute mother, enough of never knowing who her father was, enough of children disappearing and no one caring enough to find the killer, enough with drug pushers and baby beaters until one day she simply . . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/texas/houston/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1440168493ra/15940067.gif" alt="Houston commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Mitchell says if all New Adult books were like these we’d read them all the time. I’m so glad I gave Tarryn Fisher another chance. (Here’s where I make some enemies, but Honey Badger don’t care.) Tarryn Fisher did what <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1158365458?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Leah Raeder</a> tried and failed to do. She’s the real deal who wrote something gritty but did so with the most beautiful flowery prose and instead of pussyfooting around she JUST. WENT. THERE. with the dark and stormy and left <b>zero</b> apologies in her wake for anyone who didn’t like it. <i>Marrow</i> earns 3.5 Stars from me because there was a part that left me feeling a little bit of . . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/texas/houston/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1440168493ra/15940068.gif" alt="Houston commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>but I’m rounding up because I <i>really</i> enjoyed it and because that cover deserves 10 Stars all on its own. I CAN. NOT. WAIT. to see what she does with a romance novel. <br><br><b>Dear Ms. Fisher: IGNORE THE DISCLAIMER IN MY “ABOUT ME” SECTION AND PLEASE SPAM THE CRAP OUT OF ME WITH A REVIEW REQUEST FOR <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25828204-f-love?from_search=true&amp;search_version=service" rel="nofollow noopener">F*** Love</a>.</b> <br></span>
  <a data-text-id="4708241275979150851" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1264687876" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1264687876" />
    <a title="warhawke" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25494927-warhawke"><img alt="warhawke" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1431835527p2/25494927.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1264687876?book_show_action=true">Apr 26, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="warhawke" class="user" itemprop="url" name="warhawke" href="/user/show/25494927-warhawke">warhawke</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25494927-warhawke?shelf=action-thriller">action-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25494927-warhawke?shelf=dark-gritty-disturbed">dark-gritty-disturbed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1264687876" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16157281421111721514"><b>Genre: </b> Dark Thriller<br/><b>Type: </b> Standalone<br/><b>POV: </b> First Person - Female<br/><b>Rating: </b><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1423545558i/13641856.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1430401066i/14709703._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Margo Moon grew up in the derelict town called Bone Harbor where poverty and social issues was just a way of life. She lived a mundane life until the day she struck up friendship with her handsome cripple neighbor, Judah Grant. Their friendship gave her purpose and meaning in everything she did.<br/><br/><br/>One day, tragedy descended upon their small town when her young friend went missing. The event awakened something dark inside her a</span>
  <span id="freeText16157281421111721514" style="display:none"><b>Genre: </b> Dark Thriller<br><b>Type: </b> Standalone<br><b>POV: </b> First Person - Female<br><b>Rating: </b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1423545558i/13641856.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1430401066i/14709703._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Margo Moon grew up in the derelict town called Bone Harbor where poverty and social issues was just a way of life. She lived a mundane life until the day she struck up friendship with her handsome cripple neighbor, Judah Grant. Their friendship gave her purpose and meaning in everything she did.<br><br><br>One day, tragedy descended upon their small town when her young friend went missing. The event awakened something dark inside her and she found a new purpose in life that skated dangerously between what’s right and what’s best. <br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1423265644i/13602509.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>Tarryn Fisher is one of my favorite dark authors. She’s a master in writing about morally corrupted characters and made us think about the beauty within the ugliness. Marrow was one of the stories of beauty within the ugly. <br><br> <blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>I do not regret my choice; I stand by it. </b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>What Margo did (which I’m not going to elaborate because you just have to read it yourself!) may not be socially acceptable, but is it morally right? Depending on your personal belief system it could go both ways. And that’s what I love the most about this type of book – every reader could interpret/viewed/accepted the story differently. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>And I fear nothing, because there is nothing left to fear.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>I absolutely love Margo. I love seeing her transformation from a timid girl who thought she was insignificant, to the woman who found her purpose in life – albeit the purpose was slightly skewed. I also love seeing how she justified her choices while still struggling with the rationale. <br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1430401066i/14709704.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Judah was actually my favorite character in this book. I love their friendship and how he was the reason she changed whether intentional or not. He was the epitome of hope - the light to her darkness. <br><br><br>If you’ve read Mud Vein, you may notice there was one significant character from the book in this one. This character’s appearance totally messed up my conclusion of this book. If the character wasn’t present, I would have believed in one conclusion without a doubt. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“Not everyone can be saved,” he said to my tear-stained face. “Sometimes you just have to let nature take its course.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>Now, I have another one that could possibly be true. So I cannot decide which theory I want to believe in and I hate it when I doubt myself. And it was probably the author’s intention to make readers question what they want to believe by including the wild card character. But then again, even if you haven’t read Mud Vein, there is still a possibility that you would have more than one conclusion. <br><br><br>A little warning, this book is not for everyone. It is dark and contained graphic and disturbing situation. If you enjoy taking a journey in the dark corner of human psyche, you’ll probably enjoy this book as much as I did.<br><br><br> <i><b>Note:</b> You don’t need to read Mud Vein before reading this book. Even though there was a character appearance, there’s no connection in the storyline. With that said, Mud Vein is still my favorite Tarryn Fisher’s book. </i><br><br><br><br>For more reviews/reveals/giveaways visit:<br><a href="http://warhawkevault.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1412943984i/11445453.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="16157281421111721514" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_944276211" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/944276211" />
    <a title="Pavlina Read more sleep less blog❤❤  " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6603203-pavlina-read-more-sleep-less-blog"><img alt="Pavlina Read more sleep less blog❤❤  " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596881564p2/6603203.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/944276211?book_show_action=true">May 21, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pavlina Read more sleep less blog❤❤  " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pavlina Read more sleep less blog❤❤  " href="/user/show/6603203-pavlina-read-more-sleep-less-blog">Pavlina Read more sleep less blog❤❤  </a>

  <span id="freeText17769846689870878044" style="display:none"> <b> 4 STARS </b><br><br>Honestly at the beginning I didn't know how to rate this book and this is why I didn't post a review immediately!I wanted to think a little.It was really brilliant,unique,captivate and weird!This is my first book from Tarryn Fisher but so far I have heard only good things about this author!!My opinion after finishing this book??Yes she is definitely a very talented author!!I loved the writing so much and this giving the book extra points!And the fact that she managed to feel like I am a part of this story is another extra point!!Let's begin with the story now!<br><br>Margo Moon lives with her mother but it's like she is alone because her mother sell herself to men and doesn't care a lot about Margo.Soon bad things starts happen and Margo see the people around her destroy themselves.We see her pain through the book...But soon she finds a new friend that he gives light in her life, Judah!He is the only one who see the beauty in her!However because of the horror things she sees she become something like a vigilante..and I know it's not right but some part of me is with her and I envy her!!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1429553637i/14604601.jpg" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>How important is love?Everybody looking for love..First from our family and then from our friends..This story is about two so different people finding each other when they really need a company..But both they have not normal families..And here is where the thing about love comes!How children need their parents love..to comfort them.. I really liked Margo she is so brave and amazing!!I think everybody has a little of Margo inside us...I liked the fact that we see her grow through the book!Judah is Margo's friend and he is exactly what she needs!!<br><br><br><b> ”I imagine that being wanted is the greatest feeling. A feeling that solidifies your stay in this life, justifies it.” </b><br><br>If you are a fan of this author give it a try I'm sure you will love it!!I'm going to buy the book in paperback because simply I freaking love the cover!!It's simply amazing!!!I'm reading soon Mud Vein and let's hope that I like it!!! </span>

  <span id="freeText7804796474113174525" style="display:none">NEW TARRYN FISHER BOOK!! Sounds intriguing!!!!<br /><br /><i>
  <b>In the Bone there is a house. <br />In the house there is a girl. <br />In the girl there is a darkness.</b>

She lives her days feeling invisible. It’s not until she develops a friendship with her wheelchair-bound neighbor, Judah Grant, that things begin to change. When neighborhood girl, seven-year-old Neveah Anthony, goes missing, Judah sets out to help Margo uncover what happened to her. <br /><br />What Margo finds changes her, and with a new perspective on life, she’s determined to find evil and punish it–targeting rapists and child molesters, one by one. <br /><br />But hunting evil is dangerous, and Margo risks losing everything, including her own soul.<br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer18081938813627189594">First half of this book was a complete 5 Star for me. I loved Margo in the beginning. The second half took a dive to a 3 Star. I'm giving it a 4 Star rating in total. Ms. Fisher sure can write. I wish I had more time. This book should be read in a few sittings but it's Christmas time and I read like a snail already so it took me a little while. <br/><br/>If you like first person thriller type books give this one a try. I will definitely be looking out for more books by this very talented writer!</span>

<div id="review_944345752" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/944345752" />
    <a title="Sharon ∞❥ is an emotional book junkie ❥∞ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3275325-sharon-is-an-emotional-book-junkie"><img alt="Sharon ∞❥ is an emotional book junkie ❥∞ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514769932p2/3275325.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/944345752?book_show_action=true">May 21, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sharon ∞❥ is an emotional book junkie ❥∞ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sharon ∞❥ is an emotional book junkie ❥∞ " href="/user/show/3275325-sharon-is-an-emotional-book-junkie">Sharon ∞❥ is an emotional book junkie ❥∞ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/25379213-marrow">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3275325-sharon-is-an-emotional-book-junkie?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer944345752" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer880939396590712467">3.5 ★'s <br/><br/><br/><b>
  <i>Abandon all logic ye who read this book...<i></i></i>
</b><br/><br/><b>The Basics:</b><br/><br/>Margo is raised in a rundown area of town where the gangbangers, meth dealers, addicts and whores live. She only knows this too well as her mother is a whore and addict. Margo will do <i>anything</i> not to turn out that way...including making herself fat and unattractive. <br/><br/>Margo's mother has all but abandoned her. She doesn't care for her and she hardly ever speaks to her instead writing down what she wants Margo to do for her. Margo is s</span>
  <span id="freeText880939396590712467" style="display:none">3.5 ★'s <br><br><br><b>
  <i>Abandon all logic ye who read this book...<i></i></i>
</b><br><br><b>The Basics:</b><br><br>Margo is raised in a rundown area of town where the gangbangers, meth dealers, addicts and whores live. She only knows this too well as her mother is a whore and addict. Margo will do <i>anything</i> not to turn out that way...including making herself fat and unattractive. <br><br>Margo's mother has all but abandoned her. She doesn't care for her and she hardly ever speaks to her instead writing down what she wants Margo to do for her. Margo is so desperate to hear her mother's voice that she listens through the walls while her mother is entertaining. And don't even get me started on her "dad". <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1429568275i/14607091.jpg" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But...people in the neighborhood seem to like Margo and she cares for some of them as well, especially a certain wheelchair bound boy named Judah. One day, something changes and instead of just walking by, she walks <i>inside</i> his gate and that changes things because she is no longer <b>alone</b>. <br><br>Unfortunately, that's not the most significant change, oh no...it's the kidnapping and murder of a neighborhood girl. A girl that Margo was the last to see, a girl that had a bear named Bambi and dollar bills with purple hearts. A girl that Margo just can't say goodbye to...and <i>that</i> really changes things forever.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1429568275ra/14607090.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>The Thoughts:</b> <br><br>First off, this book is <b>not</b> a romance book. Sure, there's a little romantic interest but <i>that's all she wrote</i>! Secondly, OMG...<b>this is NOT a YA book</b>! I would <i>never</i> let my young children read this...maybe a mature sixteen-plus year old....<i>maybe</i>. <br><br>This book is definitely dark, definitely suspense, <i>definitely</i> psychological thriller and (IMO) definitely horror. It felt like something Stephen King would write with a little Twilight Zone thrown in and some good doses of the movie, <i>Unbreakable</i>. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1429567694ra/14606924.gif" width="300" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I think Margo was maybe sane for a few years when she was young but <i>everything</i> has taken its toll. The problem is that Margo doesn't <i>see</i> it that way...and that's even scarier!<br> <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1422563971ra/13517191.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>And that leads to the main problem...it's hard for the reader to know what's true and what isn't. <br><br>There's also an even creepier tie in with TF's other book, <i>Mud Vein</i>, and it's not a good thing. I think that <i>particular</i> person screwed up Margo even further. Unfortunately, Margo just needed to talk to someone...<i>anyone</i> and the person she talked to basically encouraged her! <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1429567694i/14606923.jpg" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>The Conclusion:</b><br><br>Am I glad I read it? I don't know. <br><br>Will I recommend it? <s>I don't know.</s> If you like this genre. <br><br>Will I read Tarryn Fisher's books in the future? I don't know. I <b>do</b> know I will scour the reviews with a magnifying glass and that kills me down to my very <i>marrow</i>! <br><br>On a positive note, I couldn't put the book down and I read it in one day. I do enjoy TF's writing and <i>The Opportunist</i> is one of my all time favorite books. <br><br>So, if you decide to read this, just go in knowing what the book is about...<b>
  <i>not</i>
</b>romance and <b>
  <i>not</i>
</b> happily ever afters! <br><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1429590262ra/14609751.gif" width="400" height="150" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <u>Favorite quotes:</u>
</b><br><br>♥ “Margo,” he says into my hair. “I’ll save you, if you save me.”<br><br>♥ “You have to be willing to be happy. Despite the mess of your life—just accept what’s happened, throw away your ideals, and create a new map of happiness to follow.”<br><br>♥ “Oh shit,” I say. “If you had another one of these things, you could walk on them.”</span>
  <a data-text-id="880939396590712467" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15163264371306840360">Long ago I decided that whatever Tarryn writes I will read it. That happened when I read Dirty Red.   <span id="freeText15163264371306840360" style="display:none">Long ago I decided that whatever Tarryn writes I will read it. That happened when I read Dirty Red. I thought, "Anyone who can make me sympathize for Leah is a magician, and I will forever read whatever she writes, even her grocery lists."<br /><br />This book is incredible (to put it simply.) The writing is sharp, and the characters are so...real. They are flawed, and rough, and broken, and damaged, and y'know what? They're characters that are so often never written about, which makes me appreciate them even more. Some characters are hard to stomach, but I think that's the point. I won't go further with that so as not to spoil you.<br /><br />This book tells the truth, and doesn't sugar coat it. Marrow hurt. The subject matter throughout this book is heavy, heavier than Mud Vein--PS for those wondering whether to read Marrow or Mud Vein first: READ MUD VEIN FIRST.<br /><br />I didn't expect to relate to Margo, but I did, and it brought me to tears. Maybe I'm crazy?<br /><br />Link to my video review: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://youtu.be/RodN0HntuPs">https://youtu.be/RodN0HntuPs</a></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1062530798" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer1906048090398711085">*before reading*<br/><br/>Um, excuse me?! How come I didn't know this book even existed? People'we been adding it to their to-read lists since May and I'm over here like O.O <br/><br/>Tarryn Fisher is a mastermind. Her writing is just...brain food I'd gladly eat until my head exploded. <br/><br/>*after reading*<br/><br/>Tarryn's books are a great weakness of mine. I usually read them the day they are released and then I wait for her new book which (obviously) doesn't have a release date. It could come out tomorrow, in a week from now </span>
  <span id="freeText1906048090398711085" style="display:none">*before reading*<br /><br />Um, excuse me?! How come I didn't know this book even existed? People'we been adding it to their to-read lists since May and I'm over here like O.O <br /><br />Tarryn Fisher is a mastermind. Her writing is just...brain food I'd gladly eat until my head exploded. <br /><br />*after reading*<br /><br />Tarryn's books are a great weakness of mine. I usually read them the day they are released and then I wait for her new book which (obviously) doesn't have a release date. It could come out tomorrow, in a week from now or next year. She never gives us the date(!!!) so I always refer to her as 'that witch'. My friends know who that is. I just want to know the date so I can mentally prepare myself but NOOOO... That witch! <br /><br />Anyway, Tarryn once again created a messed up leading lady. She has serious problems but I loved her because she was strong; she took a chance and change her life completely. Sure, sometimes it would backfire but she would pick all of her broken pieces and put herself back together. She learned from her mistakes and in the end, she found peace in who she is which I think was the most important thing. <br /><br />I liked the connection between Marrow and Mud Vein. It was really interesting and I kept waiting for those characters to pop up. Wish the creepy serial rapist/murderer from Love Me with Lies was also here. I bet Margo would love to see him. ;) <br /><br />I feel like explaining why the characters were the way they were and talking about the plot would reveal a lot of things you should experience for yourself. You just need to know Marrow will grab you right from the start and will make you question your beliefs. </span>

<div id="review_1161341121" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1161341121" />
    <a title="AleJandra" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25897549-alejandra"><img alt="AleJandra" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1488738602p2/25897549.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1161341121?book_show_action=true">Jan 08, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="AleJandra" class="user" itemprop="url" name="AleJandra" href="/user/show/25897549-alejandra">AleJandra</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25897549-alejandra?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25897549-alejandra?shelf=terror">terror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25897549-alejandra?shelf=dark-romance">dark-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25897549-alejandra?shelf=favoritos">favoritos</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25897549-alejandra?shelf=gore">gore</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1161341121" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer356044195657365534"><b>
  <u>5 <i>AND SHIT</i> STARS</u>
  <br/>
  <br/>
  <blockquote>
    <i>“The moon is wicked, jealous of the sun. People do bad things in the dark, under the hollow gaze of the moon. It’s smiling at me now, proud of my sin.”<br/><br/>"I am the essence of evil</i>
  </blockquote>
</b><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1436204877i/15431627.jpg' width='500' height='260' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Primer libro que leo de <b>Tarryn Fisher</b> y lo ame por completo. Es curioso que leyera este libro la semana que se celebra el día de las madres cuando la historia nos muestra de una manera muy cruda y real que no todas las madres merecen ser celebradas. Es lo único que diré sobre la histori</span>
  <span id="freeText356044195657365534" style="display:none"><b>
  <u>5 <i>AND SHIT</i> STARS</u>
  <br>
  <br>
  <blockquote>
    <i>“The moon is wicked, jealous of the sun. People do bad things in the dark, under the hollow gaze of the moon. It’s smiling at me now, proud of my sin.”<br><br>"I am the essence of evil</i>
  </blockquote>
</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1436204877i/15431627.jpg" width="500" height="260" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Primer libro que leo de <b>Tarryn Fisher</b> y lo ame por completo. Es curioso que leyera este libro la semana que se celebra el día de las madres cuando la historia nos muestra de una manera muy cruda y real que no todas las madres merecen ser celebradas. Es lo único que diré sobre la historia, todo lo demás será solo los sentimiento que me dejo.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"I hate that nothing can be done about the suffering of children, and that most of the world blocks out their suffering to cope with their own inability to help."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>Esta reseña va a ser un poco confusa, ya que no se si pueda expresar mis sentimientos de la manera correcta.<br><br>Empezare mencionando la explicación que tiene este libro al final, no es parte de la historia, es lo que motivo a Tarryn Fisher a escribir este libro.<br><br>Ella nos cuenta que hace tiempo vio un video en Youtube de una señora golpeado a un bebe. Yo también vi ese video cuando se hizo viral, porque una amiga lo publico en mi facebook. Yo no vi el video completo, simplemente porque no aguante ver como dañaban de esa manera a un inocente y la impotencia de no poder hacer nada para ayudarlo. Recuerdo que pensé que quizá la mujer que lo golpeaba sufría alguna enfermedad mental, también pensé en la persona que grabó el video en vez de hacer algo para ayudar a un pobre bebe. <br><br>Pero en la reflexión de Tarry Fisher ella explica en como ella miro el video completo enfocándose en el sufrimiento del bebe, no porque lo disfrutaba si no porque lo menos que ese bebe se merecía era que los demás que vimos el video sufriéramos con él. Esa anécdota llevo a esta escritora a crear a Margo, la protagonista de Marrow.<br><br>A veces leemos tantos libros, que se nos olvida que cada autor pasa por un proceso creativo diferente, y que en cada libro nos están dando algo de sí mismos. Cuando leemos alguna historia romántica es fácil entender como una autora fantasea tener una historia así.<br><br>Pero en este caso, la autora nos muestra sus demonios, esa obscuridad que algunos desarrollamos al ver las cosas malas que le suceden a personas buenas. Tarryn Fisher exorciza sus demonios plasmándolos en historias.<br><br>No sé si soy rara, pero cuando llego a ver uno de esos videos donde personas buenas en especial niños son lastimados, si me dan ganas de volverme como Margo y castigar a dichas personas. Se que no soy la única que se siente de dicha manera, obviamente nunca aremos algo al respecto porque tenemos conciencia y siendo honestos porque no queremos terminar en la cárcel. Pero eso no impide que los imaginemos, que fantaseemos con castigar de la manera más cruel y dolorosa a aquellas personas que solo viven para dañar a los demás y hacer de este un mundo mejor.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1431490831ra/14841126.gif" width="500" height="260" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Al inicio el libro es bastante triste y melancólico, también un poco confuso por los brincos en el tiempo. Pero la historia te mantiene enganchada, deseando poder terminarlo. En serio tuve que leer otro libro inmediatamente después de acabar este porque no quería que las imágenes que me causó esta historia se quedaran mucho tiempo en mi cabeza ya que son demasiado dolorosas.<br><br>Me gusto el final, a pesar que no termine de entenderlo y la verdad no quiero pasar más tiempo analizándolo. Prefiero quedarme en la negación de que en realidad Margo The Murdess tuvo su felices para siempre con Judha, Little Mo y con su oscuro pasajero (Si la historia me recordó a la serie de Dexter).<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"Sometimes, by saving someone else, you save yourself a little as well"</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>Comentario Random<br>Cuando leí <b>Never Never</b> me fascino la historia, pero la sorpresa para mí fue amar un libro de <b> Colleen Hoover</b> (No tengo nada contra ella, simplemente no soy fan de sus libros) pero al leer este libro me di cuenta que si ame tanto Never Never fue por la escritura de Tarryn Fisher, aun no estoy segura pero ella podría convertirse en mi nueva autora favorita. Ya tengo muchísimas ganas de leer más libros de ella, aunque primero debo recuperarme de este.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1431490831ra/14841127.gif" width="500" height="270" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="356044195657365534" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1307505676" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1307505676" />
    <a title="Cranky - The Book Curmudgeon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/39383783-cranky---the-book-curmudgeon"><img alt="Cranky - The Book Curmudgeon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1421782502p2/39383783.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1307505676?book_show_action=true">Jun 14, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cranky - The Book Curmudgeon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cranky - The Book Curmudgeon" href="/user/show/39383783-cranky---the-book-curmudgeon">Cranky - The Book Curmudgeon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1307505676" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14084294700899749769">***** 5 Cranky stars *****<br/><br/><img src='https://s3.amazonaws.com/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1423030270r/13578828.gif?142303027043798' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>If Mud Vein signaled Fisher’s departure from the romance genre, Marrow reinforces it. A psychological thriller, narrated through the first person point of view of Margo Moon, one of the more fascinating characters in contemporary works. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1434282403ra/15197376.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>Margo Moon: an empathetic serial killer stands in contrast to fundamental tenets in the popular, sociological imagination. Her motivation is not primal cruelty, but empathy for the victims.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1434282403ra/15197377.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>Born and raised in a place called “The Bone”,</span>
  <span id="freeText14084294700899749769" style="display:none">***** 5 Cranky stars *****<br><br><img src="https://s3.amazonaws.com/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1423030270r/13578828.gif?142303027043798" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>If Mud Vein signaled Fisher’s departure from the romance genre, Marrow reinforces it. A psychological thriller, narrated through the first person point of view of Margo Moon, one of the more fascinating characters in contemporary works. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1434282403ra/15197376.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Margo Moon: an empathetic serial killer stands in contrast to fundamental tenets in the popular, sociological imagination. Her motivation is not primal cruelty, but empathy for the victims.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1434282403ra/15197377.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Born and raised in a place called “The Bone”, a section of society where there is both a dearth of hope and justice, the only living daughter of a broken prostitute, and an absent, disinterested father, Margo is all too familiar with what is wrong in the world. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1434282403ra/15197378.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>When a young girl goes missing, Margo embarks on an investigation with her one and only friend, Judah, to get justice for a child that is otherwise disposable. Facing the age old dilemma of human laws versus moral ones, Margo dispenses an Old Testament form of punishment to the guilty.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1434282403ra/15197379.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Written in Fisher’s trademark sparse, multi-layered, and poetic prose, Marrow is an uncomfortable, but riveting read. One of Fisher’s greatest strengths is her observations on the darker impulses of human nature where she makes the broken understandable. You might not relate to them, nor agree with their actions, but she makes you understand why they do the things that they do.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1434282403ra/15197380.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>The few criticisms I have of this book are plot, pacing, and character consistency. It plateaus somewhat in the middle and the connection with Fisher’s earlier work, Mud Vein, diverts Margo’s story. At this point, I questioned character consistency and thought it skirted with deus ex machina. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1434282602ra/15197418.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>If you like psychological thrillers, complex characters, and being outside your comfort zone, I highly recommend Marrow. Margo Moon will live long in the memory and is one of my favorite characters of Tarryn Fisher’s works.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1434282404ra/15197382.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br></span>

<div id="review_944535479" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/944535479" />
    <a title="Serena" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15579788-serena"><img alt="Serena" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605724905p2/15579788.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/944535479?book_show_action=true">May 21, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Serena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Serena" href="/user/show/15579788-serena">Serena</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15579788-serena?shelf=all-time-favorites">all-time-favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer944535479" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10628907067584192599">Tarryn Fisher is so talented and every single story she writes is unique and beautiful. When you pick up one of her novels, you know that she is going to give you her all, make you think, and ache for more in the process. Her characters are real and complex. Although Mud Vein was my top read of 2014, Marrow will easily slide into that current spot for 2015. When you meet Margo, you will see why. Margo is someone we all want to be like. You root for her because she is doing what we sometimes thin</span>
  <span id="freeText10628907067584192599" style="display:none">Tarryn Fisher is so talented and every single story she writes is unique and beautiful. When you pick up one of her novels, you know that she is going to give you her all, make you think, and ache for more in the process. Her characters are real and complex. Although Mud Vein was my top read of 2014, Marrow will easily slide into that current spot for 2015. When you meet Margo, you will see why. Margo is someone we all want to be like. You root for her because she is doing what we sometimes think. I absolutely love the character development and getting to know Margo from a young age. You really get a sense of who she is and where she came from. I loved Judah because he is caring, witty and his friendship pulls her out of the darkness. <br /><br />Tarryn's writing reminds me a lot of Gillian Flynn. It is mysterious, dark and complex. Just when you think you know where it is going, she throws in another twist. This book kept me on the edge of my seat and left me wanting more. My mind is still processing the story and it will be for weeks. I highly recommend this book as your next read.<br /><br />A few of my favorite quotes from Marrow:<br /><br />“You must not let hatred destroy you. You will lose your soul,” she says. <br />I don’t look at her as I walk back to the boy who she says gives me hope. I want to tell her that she need not worry about my soul. This boy will save it. <br /><br />Sadness is an emotion you can trust. It is stronger than all of the other emotions. It makes happiness look fickle and untrustworthy. It pervades, lasts longer, and replaces the good feelings with such an eloquent ease you don’t even feel the shift until you are suddenly wrapped in its chains. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10628907067584192599" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
