<div id="review_1157717403" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1157717403" />
    <a title="Melanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie"><img alt="Melanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577914102p2/3030788.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1157717403?book_show_action=true">Jan 05, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanie" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie">Melanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=signed">signed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=dark">dark</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1157717403" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7664167801162045854"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1449013266i/17220380._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This book is beautifully written. So beautiful it hurts and makes you feel very real things. This is probably why I hold Tarryn Fisher's novels in such high regards. She has an indisputable talent. I collapsed into <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/904424952?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>Mud Vein's</a> words while it healed some of my own broken pieces. It's my favorite book to date. <br/><br/>This is a wonderful story that perfectly describes love and how we all want it no matter how many times we tell ourselves we don't. The story does show the love between two perfectly imperfec</span>
  <span id="freeText7664167801162045854" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1449013266i/17220380._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This book is beautifully written. So beautiful it hurts and makes you feel very real things. This is probably why I hold Tarryn Fisher's novels in such high regards. She has an indisputable talent. I collapsed into <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/904424952?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Mud Vein's</a> words while it healed some of my own broken pieces. It's my favorite book to date. <br><br>This is a wonderful story that perfectly describes love and how we all want it no matter how many times we tell ourselves we don't. The story does show the love between two perfectly imperfect strangers that find each other when they need it most, but it mostly highlights on the ugly love of family. How badly children want/need love, and how sometimes they just cannot get it. How some people only exist to hurt others. How we have an awful downward spiral where these poor helpless children learn how to "love" from these parents who never learned how to love. How some aren't lucky enough to escape the abuse except for death. This isn't a light read, but it is eye opening and real. Unfortunately, the beautifully written words of this book did not give me the catharsis <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/904424952?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Mud Vein</a> did. <br><br><b><u>Major spoilers are ahead,</u> so please do not continue on with this review if you want to experience the twists for yourself. </b><br><br>After I read this, something was screaming at me. The synopsis of this book is not correct: <i>"What Margo finds changes her, and with a new perspective on life, she’s determined to find evil and punish it–targeting rapists and child molesters, one by one."</i><br><br>I'm not sure what Tarryn Fisher's definition of child molester is, but it is not cohesive with the legal definition: <i>"Child molestation is a crime involving a range of indecent or sexual activities between an adult and a child, usually under the age of 14."</i><br><br>Margo kills many people in this book (a child beater, a child killer/accomplice, adult potential rapist), but not one of them is a known child molester. This irks me to no end. The Wikipedia page does not even capture physical abuse in the concept of child molestation. How could the most powerful writer I've ever read mess this up? Did I skip over pages? Am I using the wrong definition? Is she using a super archaic form of the word molest? Targeting one by one is a little off putting too. She kills three and wounds one so badly he will wish for death. I think targeting one by one is a little bit of a stretch. Especially considering two of these kills literally fell into her lap right before her eyes. <br><br>The next thing I didn't like was Judah not being real. Please Lord, make this poor cripple boy with a beautiful soul that saved Margo be real. I understand the healing Margo received from him does not depend on him being real or not, but what a sad fucking story if he really wasn't real. My heart breaks over and over for Margo. <br><br>My heart swelled at the other twist in this book. No, it exploded. Senna, my Senna from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/904424952?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Mud Vein</a>. The most heart wrenching character I've ever read about. The start of her pain came from Margo's mistake. While Margo was torturing a man who rapes women, she gets over confident and reckless. The man overpowers her and suddenly she's not in control of the situation. The man that Margo was careless with delivered the vengeance on Senna. I was crushed, broken and begging for more all over again. I was blindsided, then overcome with joy from this beautiful correlation of events. Ironically, Margo is in the same mental hospital that Senna blocked out of her mind, so she realizes what has happened. This also gave me hope for Judah being real, because of the events Dr. Elgin executed in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/904424952?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Mud Vein</a>. Please, oh please. Margo deserves an Isaac too. <br><br>Everyone that reads this book is going to perceive it differently. They are going to take from it many different things. Many will even have different endings, and that's beautiful all in itself. <br><br>Even though I'm only giving this book four stars, I loved it.<br><br>Tarryn, you and your words have ruined me for other authors.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7664167801162045854" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1646874498" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1646874498" />
    <a title="Hayley ☾ (TheVillainousReader)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22062635-hayley-thevillainousreader"><img alt="Hayley ☾ (TheVillainousReader)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1595882462p2/22062635.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1646874498?book_show_action=true">May 23, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hayley ☾ (TheVillainousReader)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hayley ☾ (TheVillainousReader)" href="/user/show/22062635-hayley-thevillainousreader">Hayley ☾ (TheVillainousReader)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781511682763" href="/book/show/25378074-marrow">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22062635-hayley-thevillainousreader?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22062635-hayley-thevillainousreader?shelf=badass-females">badass-females</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22062635-hayley-thevillainousreader?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22062635-hayley-thevillainousreader?shelf=reread-worthy">reread-worthy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22062635-hayley-thevillainousreader?shelf=dark">dark</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1646874498" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4192375730557136218"><i>Rrrrrr ta ta ta. My marrow cries out, reminding me of who I am. I am Margo Moon. I am a murderess. I believe in poetic vengeance.</i><br/><br/><b>The first time I read this book it sang to my soul. After the second time I've decided that it's my all time favorite book.</b><br/><br/>I really believe that Marrow is best to go into blind so I'm going to try and keep my review vague while trying to capture how much this book affected me. Is that even possible?! I guess we'll see..<br/><br/><i>"Just tell me one thing," he says. "Does you heart</i></span>
  <span id="freeText4192375730557136218" style="display:none"><i>Rrrrrr ta ta ta. My marrow cries out, reminding me of who I am. I am Margo Moon. I am a murderess. I believe in poetic vengeance.</i><br /><br /><b>The first time I read this book it sang to my soul. After the second time I've decided that it's my all time favorite book.</b><br /><br />I really believe that Marrow is best to go into blind so I'm going to try and keep my review vague while trying to capture how much this book affected me. Is that even possible?! I guess we'll see..<br /><br /><i>"Just tell me one thing," he says. "Does you heart still... beat with the ache and pain there? Does it still beat?<br />"Yes," I say. <br />"That's because humans are built to live with pain. Weak people let their pain choke them to a slow, emotional death. Strong people use that pain, Margo. They use it as fuel."</i><br /><br />Marrow feeds my soul. It's hauntingly tragic and beautiful. The world is a fucked up place. Many of us see evil in the world and feel helpless to stop it, that it is so much bigger than us so we turn away. I'm guilty of this. The innocent suffer at the hands of the sick, greedy and cruel. You know it, I know it and Tarry Fisher sure as hell knows it. From the horrors and injustice <a href="http://www.tarrynfisher.com/why-i-wrote-marrow/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tarryn</a> has seen in the world she created Margo. <br /><br />Margo grew up in a poor neighborhood in a house that ate the souls of everyone who lived there. She is a human shaped by sorrow and loneliness. A child raised in darkness. She saw the injustice in the world, the way the innocent are wronged and brutalized and she took vengeance into her own hands. In her bright blue Docs she made those assholes pay and I went happily along for the ride, encouraging her at every turn of the page, whispering that she had a right to punish them for their evil because her vengeance was mine. <br /><br />While Margo is vengeance and darkness, Judah is light and goodness. Their relationship is heartbreakingly beautiful. The wicked, ugly murderess and the beautiful wheelchair-bound boy desperately trying to save each other. <br /><br /><i>Judah and I outgrow the rest of the Bone and cleave to one another. Nothing is better than the discovery of another living, breathing human, who fights the same as you do, loves the same as you do, and understand you with such clarity it feels erotic. A friendship between the fat, ugly girl and the crippled, handsome boy.</i><br /><br />True to Tarryn fashion this book hit me so much deeper than I first imagined. It made me reevaluate myself, degrees of evils and contemplate loneliness. It's written so beautifully that it is truly a work of art. The words of Marrow will stay with me forever. It's one of those books you consume in one sitting to then reread painstakingly slow, absorbing every detail. <br /><br /><i>The moon is wicked, jealous of the sun. People do bad things in the dark, under the hollow gaze of the moon. It’s smiling at me now, proud of my sin." </i></span>
  <a data-text-id="4192375730557136218" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer944150322" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10328474759702118791"><br/><b>Recent Post-Reading Feelings:</b><br/><br/>I "literally" HAVE NO IDEA and if I SHOULD HAVE AN IDEA?<br/><br/>I literally don't know WHAT is REAL or NOT.<br/><br/>I know this was on purpose.<br/><br/>This is Tarryn playing with your head in the most fucked up way you can ever imagine... and guess what?<br/><br/>I literally have NO IDEA is that's a good thing or a bad thing.<br/><br/>NO RATING for now.<br/><br/> <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1430537612i/14726308.gif' width='' height='' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>_________________________<br/><br/><b>Now that I'm calm enough:</b><br/><br/>When I start reading this book I was really excited. I loved all the quotes, every piece of it. I was feeling</span>
  <span id="freeText10328474759702118791" style="display:none"><br><b>Recent Post-Reading Feelings:</b><br><br>I "literally" HAVE NO IDEA and if I SHOULD HAVE AN IDEA?<br><br>I literally don't know WHAT is REAL or NOT.<br><br>I know this was on purpose.<br><br>This is Tarryn playing with your head in the most fucked up way you can ever imagine... and guess what?<br><br>I literally have NO IDEA is that's a good thing or a bad thing.<br><br>NO RATING for now.<br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1430537612i/14726308.gif" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>_________________________<br><br><b>Now that I'm calm enough:</b><br><br>When I start reading this book I was really excited. I loved all the quotes, every piece of it. I was feeling Margo. I identified with her in a way I never identified with others Tarryn's characters. <br><br>And then, like at the middle of it, everything when down to hill.<br><br>I got the feeling and the whole idea of the book, but for me it was implausible the way the things were going. To keep reading and constantly think about how that couldn't be like that, or like that, was terrible for me.<br><br>I think if you are going to write a book about murder, you really have to think about all possibilities to make your story credible.I know you can hypothetically give some excuses about the way everything happened but that's not the way it should be. <br><br>When I read Thief, and I compare some facts with The Opportunist, the same thing happened to me. There was a line who change the WHOLE PLOT: what Olivia overheard through the door, and I really wanted to justify it. And I did it.But it was like a spine in your finger. You just can't ignore it. Because that kind of things are too forced. You're creating too much drama just to go with the flow, just to try to impact the reader, and no caring about the real facts. And some of us, really care about it. (Same thing with Hoover so there is not surprise they're best friends.) <br><br>When I read the end, I was like: OMG if this is what I think it is,Tarryn is a genius. But then, she said in a chat that it wasn't like that so, I was dissapointed. <br><br>I still think she is an unique author. This whole idea is amazing, genius. I just think she really needs to be careful. You can create drama, but authors need reinforcing the pillars on which it is made.<br><br><br><br><br><br><br> <br><br></span>

<div id="review_944816789" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/944816789" />
    <a title=" Megan • Reading Books Like a Boss (book blog)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2607684-megan-reading-books-like-a-boss-book-blog"><img alt=" Megan • Reading Books Like a Boss (book blog)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1486609762p2/2607684.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/944816789?book_show_action=true">May 22, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" Megan • Reading Books Like a Boss (book blog)" class="user" itemprop="url" name=" Megan • Reading Books Like a Boss (book blog)" href="/user/show/2607684-megan-reading-books-like-a-boss-book-blog"> Megan • Reading Books Like a Boss (book blog)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/25379213-marrow">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2607684-megan-reading-books-like-a-boss-book-blog?shelf=2015-releases">2015-releases</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer944816789" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6946740939815455476"><a href='http://bit.ly/1QeAC3G' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img width='100%' src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1429653127i/14617690._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <em>I can't stay the way I am. I don't remember what it's like to be free. To be wide open without fear. I need something to break me. Just enough so that I have new pieces to work with—make them into something else.</em>
</blockquote><br/><strong>Tarryn Fisher takes readers to a dark, moldy, dreary place deep in the recesses of the human condition in <em>Marrow</em>.</strong> Fisher's beautifully dark writing style is on full display in this psychological thriller about an emotionally disturbed and deeply unsettled girl and her transformat</span>
  <span id="freeText6946740939815455476" style="display:none"><a href="http://bit.ly/1QeAC3G" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img width="100%" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1429653127i/14617690._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><blockquote>
  <em>I can't stay the way I am. I don't remember what it's like to be free. To be wide open without fear. I need something to break me. Just enough so that I have new pieces to work with—make them into something else.</em>
</blockquote><br><strong>Tarryn Fisher takes readers to a dark, moldy, dreary place deep in the recesses of the human condition in <em>Marrow</em>.</strong> Fisher's beautifully dark writing style is on full display in this psychological thriller about an emotionally disturbed and deeply unsettled girl and her transformation into a vigilante murderess.<br><br>Margo Moon grew up in a loveless house with a mentally ill mother who was more absent than present, more wrapped up in her own illness than with her daughter's well-being. After nearly a decade of being blatantly ignored, emotionally abused, and nearly starved, Margo meets a friend named Judah who lives down the street. A boy she's always seen but never spoken to.<br><br>Judah empowers Margo. This timid, shy, "fat" girl begins to change into someone else. Their friendship combined with tragedy ignites a desire deep within Margo, perhaps <strong>uncovering the girl who's always dwelled inside of her skin, in her bones, in her marrow. The darkness becomes her.</strong><br><blockquote>
  <em>"I don't know which person is the imposter. I am either Margo of the Bone, or this new thing, this murderer. Or maybe I've always been her, this vile, wicked person; she was just there, simmering beneath the surface, waiting for me to act on my impulses."</em>
</blockquote><br>The Bone is a character in and of itself. Judah says that the Bone is in their marrow. It's buried deep within them and is a part of who they are. The dark, drab neighborhood Margo was raised in with people like Mo, the drug dealer, and Mother Mary, the creepy old woman who knows when you will die, plays a vital role in Margo and Judah's lives. It motivates Margo to make many of the choices and decisions she makes and is always in the back of her mind, a reminder who where she came from. Fisher describes this neighborhood so incredibly well to where I could feel the oppression and the heaviness of the setting.<br><br>One of the things I always enjoy about Tarryn Fisher's books are her characters. Margo is an example of Fisher's ability to hone and craft a character down to the smallest detail. <strong>There is something strikingly off about her, yet I found myself rooting for her.</strong> I liked how Margo did not put herself in the same category as the other "bad" serial killers. She felt her reasons for murdering people were justified, unlike the Ted Bundy's of the world.<br><blockquote>
  <em>"I don't want to hurt people, I don't have an innate need to, but they must be punished. That's what I do, or what I tell myself I do. I punish. I feel responsible for it. An eye for an eye. A beating for a beating. A burn for a burn. I have a conscience. It's different from the average person, but at least it's still there. "</em>
</blockquote><br>Margo was complex and downright chilling. Despite the sadness of her upbringing and the complete lack of love in her life, she never complained about any of it. She was resilient, a phoenix rising from the ashes, and used the inequities in her life as a catalyst. I like how she evolved from the beginning of the book to the very last page.<br><blockquote>
  <em>"I don't feel a single thing. Strange, I crack my neck as I leave the alley. I have to stop fucking killing people."</em>
</blockquote><br><strong>While I did like this book, I found that I could put it down and walk away.</strong> Don't get me wrong, I wanted to know where Margo's path of destruction would take her and how she evolved. But <em>Marrow</em> didn't hold me hostage like I wanted it to. This is a very character-driven book with a lot of internal dialogue, which is something I love and do not fault books for.  But keeping in mind the quiet nature of the book, I was not riveted and found several parts of the book to be a bit slow.<br><br>If you're looking for a thriller that is mind-bendy, then you should read Marrow. I'd love to know your thoughts on the "nugget of mystery" Tarryn Fisher leaves in readers' hands. I'm still going back and forth as to what I think on this "mystery." For those who have read Marrow -- <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[OMG, was Judah real or not? I have so much I want to say on this front. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>And one more thing: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I did cry in this book because of Mud Vein. If you've read Mud Vein, you might cry too. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><i>* I received an advanced copy from the author in exchange for an honest review.</i><br><br><strong>If you've read Marrow and would like to talk about it, you can join the <a href="https://www.facebook.com/groups/1598897223690850" rel="nofollow noopener">Marrow Discussion Group on Facebook</a>. </strong>Lots of people have had some great discussions already. #BabyImCrazy<br><br><a href="http://bit.ly/1QeAC3G" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1429653090i/14617688._SY540_.jpg" alt="Marrow by Tarryn Fisher" width="100%" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>____________________________________________<br>★ Check out my list of <a href="http://readingbookslikeaboss.com/bookreleases/" rel="nofollow noopener">UPCOMING BOOK RELEASES!!</a><br>____________________________________________<br><br><strong>Find more of my reviews &amp; other bookish things here:<br>✥ <a href="http://bit.ly/1QeAC3G" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Read this review on the blog!</a><br>✥ My blog <a href="http://readingbookslikeaboss.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Reading Books Like a Boss</a><br>✥ Like on <a href="https://www.facebook.com/ReadingBooksLikeABoss" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a><br>✥ Follow on <a href="http://twitter.com/ireadlikeaboss" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a><br>✥ Pin with me on <a href="http://pinterest.com/ireadlikeaboss" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a><br>✥ Follow on <a href="http://instagram.com/ireadlikeaboss" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a><br>✥ Subscribe by <a href="http://readingbookslikeaboss.us10.list-manage.com/subscribe/post?u=e1db0261647306d53aef66844&amp;id=e10ebb3cc7" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Email</a><br></strong><br><a href="http://readingbookslikeaboss.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

<div id="review_1275791347" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1275791347" />
    <a title="Kirsten" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23049700-kirsten"><img alt="Kirsten" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1426126650p2/23049700.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1275791347?book_show_action=true">May 09, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kirsten" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kirsten" href="/user/show/23049700-kirsten">Kirsten</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23049700-kirsten?shelf=total-mind-fuck">total-mind-fuck</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23049700-kirsten?shelf=it-s-dark-in-here">it-s-dark-in-here</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23049700-kirsten?shelf=kickass-heroine">kickass-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23049700-kirsten?shelf=edge-of-my-seat">edge-of-my-seat</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1275791347" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14586613993700362303"><b>***Too tough to rate***</b><br/><br/><a href='http://s1278.photobucket.com/user/kabbaje6/media/Collages/image.jpg1_zpsutgo4foy.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433149511i/15056055.jpg' alt=' photo image.jpg1_zpsutgo4foy.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>By no means does my <i>non-rating</i> mean negativity. If you were to <b>make</b> me rate this book, it would be on the upper end. However, I think my head is just such a mess after not only reading this, but <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18246727.Mud_Vein' title='Mud Vein by Tarryn Fisher' rel='nofollow noopener'> Mud Vein</a> recently, that at least for now I am unable to settle for a solid representation.<br/><br/>As you can tell by the collage it seems like I put in a bunch of totally random pictures and just stuck them all together. Believe me, I had more, but when I finished, it looked cluttered</span>
  <span id="freeText14586613993700362303" style="display:none"><b>***Too tough to rate***</b><br><br><a href="http://s1278.photobucket.com/user/kabbaje6/media/Collages/image.jpg1_zpsutgo4foy.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433149511i/15056055.jpg" alt=" photo image.jpg1_zpsutgo4foy.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>By no means does my <i>non-rating</i> mean negativity. If you were to <b>make</b> me rate this book, it would be on the upper end. However, I think my head is just such a mess after not only reading this, but <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18246727.Mud_Vein" title="Mud Vein by Tarryn Fisher" rel="nofollow noopener"> Mud Vein</a> recently, that at least for now I am unable to settle for a solid representation.<br><br>As you can tell by the collage it seems like I put in a bunch of totally random pictures and just stuck them all together. Believe me, I had more, but when I finished, it looked cluttered and there was just too much going on, so I had to scale it back. In hindsight, the other graphic was probably more accurate, as all the things were like their own character in this book, and yet made me feel the same way...overwhelmed. <br><br>Let's start with what this book is about.<br><br>I think <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22253643.Marrow" title="Marrow by Tarryn Fisher" rel="nofollow noopener"> Marrow</a>, can be perceived by everyone differently. And I like that aspect. <br><br>For me, this was about a very broken girl turned vigilante. Margo is the main character and it goes through her life from the age of 13 to 21. She grew up in Bone Harbor, which everyone there refers to as <i>the Bone</i>, a destitute place where no one would want to live. She has names for different houses on her street, and calls her house <i>the eating house</i>. Her mother is awful and her life is really sad. A turning point in her life happens when a young girl who she has befriended goes missing. <br><br>She finds herself coming across some scenes that will shock and horrify. She realizes that she can be the one to stop these situations and does something about it. <br><br><a href="http://s1278.photobucket.com/user/kabbaje6/media/Collages/image.jpg2_zps0p4bnw1o.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433149511i/15056056.jpg" alt=" photo image.jpg2_zps0p4bnw1o.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I will not go into anymore of what this book is about. Simply put, I can't. Not only do I have no clue, but this is the epitome of one of the books you'd have to read to get the full effect and come to your own conclusion. <br><br><a href="http://s1278.photobucket.com/user/kabbaje6/media/Collages/imagejpg3_zpsdfa8f0b7.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1420627563i/13246214.jpg" alt=" photo imagejpg3_zpsdfa8f0b7.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I apologize if you don't understand the reference, but I am sure at one time you have related to something similar. <br><br>David Lynch is one of my favorite directors and makes awesome mindfuck movies (Blue Velvet, Lost Highway, Mulholland Drive). His mind is fascinating. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5410816.Tarryn_Fisher" title="Tarryn Fisher" rel="nofollow noopener"> Tarryn Fisher</a>'s last two books reminded me of his films. They're kind of dark, gritty, and fuck with your head. The entire time you are watching them you ask yourself over and over, "What is going on?", "What is the point to all of this?", and "Why am I still watching this when I'm so confused?". Which then leads to... "I can't stop watching this.", "Everything will make sense soon.", and "I have to find out what happens". In the end, you're not totally sure what to think. You loved and hated it simultaneously because it messed with you so bad. Even though you still are puzzled, you appreciate the complex mind that came up with such a bizarre and brilliant story. <br><br>And <i>that</i> is the best way I can describe <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22253643.Marrow" title="Marrow by Tarryn Fisher" rel="nofollow noopener"> Marrow</a>, and I hope it helps.<br><br><br>If you've read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18246727.Mud_Vein" title="Mud Vein by Tarryn Fisher" rel="nofollow noopener"> Mud Vein</a>, you are able to find out where <b>pink zippos</b> came from. And thank goodness for that! One less thing, I suppose. :) <br><br>If at all possible, I think you will enjoy this more if you read it with someone. The dialogue and the theories you come up with cannot only be helpful, but comical as well (because you'll both feel crazy). <br><br><i>Thanks Michelle, for being my crazy buddy! </i> <br></span>
  <a data-text-id="14586613993700362303" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3511883888?book_show_action=true">Aug 23, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aj the Ravenous Reader" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader">Aj the Ravenous Reader</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3511883888" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11555594925132633580">Woah! What did I just read?! I thought Tarryn Fisher only wrote about messed up, morally flawed characters and their annoying problems. But this, this is the last thing I expected from her.<br/><br/>Here's a girl who grew up with one shitty parent because the other one does not even want to acknowledge her existence, in a shitty house, in a shitty neighborhood and still managed to grow up a very decent person, still messed up but in a very useful way. I mean, she does attempt murder people and is even oft</span>
  <span id="freeText11555594925132633580" style="display:none">Woah! What did I just read?! I thought Tarryn Fisher only wrote about messed up, morally flawed characters and their annoying problems. But this, this is the last thing I expected from her.<br /><br />Here's a girl who grew up with one shitty parent because the other one does not even want to acknowledge her existence, in a shitty house, in a shitty neighborhood and still managed to grow up a very decent person, still messed up but in a very useful way. I mean, she does attempt murder people and is even often successful but it's all for a good cause. <br /><br />And yet it was written very lyrically. It's really unfathomable how the author made it work. It is poetic, emotional, gripping, and thought provoking. I could hug her for bringing to attention the abuse and suffering children endure from their own parents. Her Afterword is a gem too, this entire novel is and now <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5410816.Tarryn_Fisher" title="Tarryn Fisher" rel="nofollow noopener">Tarryn Fisher</a> is definitely another author/hero for me!<br /></span>

<div id="review_2197096180" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2197096180" />
    <a title="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell"><img alt="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1584062476p2/2190064.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2197096180?book_show_action=true">Dec 04, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" href="/user/show/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell">Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/25379213-marrow">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=the-lost-girls">the-lost-girls</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=dark-and-twisted">dark-and-twisted</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2197096180" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9632924745381844653"><a href='http://readasaurus.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><a href='https://www.instagram.com/neniagram/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Instagram</a> || <a href='https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twitter</a> || <a href='https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Facebook</a> || <a href='http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS' rel='nofollow noopener'>Amazon</a> || <a href='https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Pinterest</a><br/><br/><br/>🌟 I read this for the Yule Bingo Challenge, for the category of <i>Snape: morally grey character</i>. For more info on this challenge, <a href='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1512084609i/24572523._SY540_.jpg' rel='nofollow noopener'>click here</a>. 🌟<br/><br/><br/><br/>Lots of authors want to write "dark" and "gritty," but few have the muscle to pull it off. Not Tarryn Fisher. Ever since reading <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2193777550' rel='nofollow noopener'>MUD VEIN</a>, I've found myself pleasantly surprised by her wide cast of flawed characters and intricately plotted stories. MUD VEIN had some weaknesses, in that it was trying</span>
  <span id="freeText9632924745381844653" style="display:none"><a href="http://readasaurus.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="https://www.instagram.com/neniagram/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> || <a href="https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> || <a href="https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> || <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon</a> || <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a><br><br><br>🌟 I read this for the Yule Bingo Challenge, for the category of <i>Snape: morally grey character</i>. For more info on this challenge, <a href="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1512084609i/24572523._SY540_.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">click here</a>. 🌟<br><br><br><br>Lots of authors want to write "dark" and "gritty," but few have the muscle to pull it off. Not Tarryn Fisher. Ever since reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2193777550" rel="nofollow noopener">MUD VEIN</a>, I've found myself pleasantly surprised by her wide cast of flawed characters and intricately plotted stories. MUD VEIN had some weaknesses, in that it was trying <i>too </i>hard to be twisty and suspenseful to the point where one had to suspend one's disbelief, but the ride was thrilling and beguiling. I wanted to read more.<br><br><br><br>Like MUD VEIN, MARROW is also built around suspense and features a heroine who is not very likable but is also highly sympathetic. Margo is a girl who lives in a low-income suburb in Seattle called "the Bone." Many of the people there are involved in petty crime of some form or another. They're the types of people who slip through the cracks, who don't report crimes because the deck is stacked against them.<br><br><br><br>Margo's mother is a prostitute and resents her existence. The two of them live in a house that Margo calls "the eating house" - because it's devouring her slowly, I guess. We follow her from young girl to young woman, and as she gets older, she becomes more and more aware of the injustices that occur in the Bone, and it slowly makes her angrier and angrier - until she loses it, and decides to take matters into her own hands. Her journey is utterly fascinating. I haven't been this engrossed by a heroine since Gillian Flynn's GONE GIRL. It's got that same sort of "descent" if you know what I mean.<br><br><br><br>MARROW is definitely not for the faint of heart, but if you enjoy dark stories and tales of suspense, with anti-heroes and revenge, this will be a good story for you. It reminded me of Caroline Kepnes's YOU and Jeff Lindsay's DARKLY DREAMING DEXTER in many ways, and I think there's a lot of crossover appeal for readers who enjoyed those stories. It has that same sense of morality play meets procedural drama. I can't wait to read the rest of this author's books.<br><br><br><br>P.S. Characters from MUD VEIN appear in this book. I picked up on some of the clues early on and wasn't sure if it was meant to be a sneaky Easter Egg - but it was! And then it turned into a full-on <i>cameo</i>. I was so excited, I literally bounced in my chair. I love it when authors do this. <br><br><br><br>4.5 stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="9632924745381844653" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2294002951" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2294002951" />
    <a title="Stormi (Bewitched Reader)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12516485-stormi-bewitched-reader"><img alt="Stormi (Bewitched Reader)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1523456984p2/12516485.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2294002951?book_show_action=true">Feb 22, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stormi (Bewitched Reader)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stormi (Bewitched Reader)" href="/user/show/12516485-stormi-bewitched-reader">Stormi (Bewitched Reader)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/25379213-marrow">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12516485-stormi-bewitched-reader?shelf=thrillers">thrillers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2294002951" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2938779072746201545">I heard about Tarryn Fisher in Colleen Hoover's CoHorts group and everyone raves about how amazing her books are. I felt like this book had a very slow start and I kept waiting for it to pick up. It did pick up a little bit, but I still contemplated putting it down and labeling it as a DNF several times throughout the book. This was a very twisty and dark read. I felt like it was quite unique and I still have questions about Judah. There are many people who will absolutely love this book, but it</span>
  <span id="freeText2938779072746201545" style="display:none">I heard about Tarryn Fisher in Colleen Hoover's CoHorts group and everyone raves about how amazing her books are. I felt like this book had a very slow start and I kept waiting for it to pick up. It did pick up a little bit, but I still contemplated putting it down and labeling it as a DNF several times throughout the book. This was a very twisty and dark read. I felt like it was quite unique and I still have questions about Judah. There are many people who will absolutely love this book, but it isn't for me. I still think I will give some of Tarryn's other books a chance because their blurbs have caught my attention.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2938779072746201545" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<li class='cover' id='bookCover_51007311'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/51007311-heart-bones"><img alt="Heart Bones" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1580936060l/51007311._SX98_.jpg" />

<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('erID3Lse5BNlEa9Z7jIVyH8b+QuVYzppRKCMiS3bH9u/toT7WnbT5Ks1O7hEeUtJ2B5nseDkHpZzrc3Skxsaqg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('IX63561vfRaJw5RKtk47ykKItcDu162q97r9jw9OdpDkejDATAdK4UfnAKscBWVL5Y0reptQiVXAt7zUsY5z4Q==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer16558065302256003151">I would like to write a novel that every, single person loves, but not even J.K. Rowling could do that. Instead, I try to write stories that pull on people's emotions. I believe that sadness is the most powerful emotion, and swirled with regret the two become a dominating force. I love villains. Three of my favorites are Mother Gothel, Gaston and the Evil Queen who all suffered from a pretty wicke</span>
  <span id="freeText16558065302256003151" style="display:none">I would like to write a novel that every, single person loves, but not even J.K. Rowling could do that. Instead, I try to write stories that pull on people's emotions. I believe that sadness is the most powerful emotion, and swirled with regret the two become a dominating force. I love villains. Three of my favorites are Mother Gothel, Gaston and the Evil Queen who all suffered from a pretty wicked case of vanity (like me). I like to make these personality types the center of my stories. <br />I love rain, Coke, Starbucks and sarcasm. I hate bad adjectives and the word "smolder". If you read my book-I love you. If you hate my book-I still love you, but please don't be mean to me; I'm half badass, half cry baby. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16558065302256003151" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
